      <p><b>Mauritius</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span></span>(<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>)<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span></span>-/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Mauritius.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/En-us-Mauritius.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Mauritius.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">mə-<span style="font-size:90%">RISH</span>-(ee-)əs, maw-</i></a>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Maurice</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[mɔʁis, moʁis]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:LL-Q150_(fra)-Jules78120-Maurice.wav" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/LL-Q150_%28fra%29-Jules78120-Maurice.wav" class="internal" title="LL-Q150 (fra)-Jules78120-Maurice.wav">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <a href="/wiki/Morisyen_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Morisyen language">Morisyen</a>: <i lang="mfe">Moris</i> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Appendix:Mauritian_Creole_pronunciation" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:Appendix:Mauritian Creole pronunciation">[moʁis]</a>), officially the <b>Republic of Mauritius</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/Island_nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Island nation">island nation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> about 2,000 kilometres (1,200&nbsp;mi) off the southeast coast of the <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> continent, east of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. It includes the main island (also called Mauritius), as well as and <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agal%C3%A9ga" title="Agaléga">Agaléga</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Brandon" title="St. Brandon">St. Brandon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ICJ_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICJ-11">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> The islands of Mauritius and Rodrigues, along with nearby <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">French overseas department</a>), are part of the <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarene Islands</a>. The capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Port_Louis" title="Port Louis">Port Louis</a>, is located on Mauritius, where most of the population is concentrated. The country spans 2,040 square kilometres (790&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and has an <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> covering 2.3 million square kilometres.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By some accounts, Arab sailors were the first to discover the uninhabited island, around 975, and they called it <i>Dina Arobi</i>, but this has not been confirmed. The earliest confirmed discovery was in 1507 by Portuguese sailors, who otherwise took little interest in the islands. The Dutch took possession in 1598, establishing a succession of short-lived settlements over a period of about 120 years, before abandoning their efforts in 1710. France took control in 1715, renaming it <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a>. In 1810, the island <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Isle_de_France" title="Invasion of Isle de France">was seized</a> by <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Great Britain</a>, and four years later France <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1814)" title="Treaty of Paris (1814)">ceded Mauritius and its dependencies</a> to Britain. As a British colony, Mauritius included Rodrigues, Agalega, St. Brandon, <a href="/wiki/Tromelin_Island" title="Tromelin Island">Tromelin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a>, and, until 1906, the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ICJ_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICJ-11">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PCA_Memorial_Vol_1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCA_Memorial_Vol_1-14">[12]</a></sup> Sovereignty over Tromelin is disputed between Mauritius and France, as it was not specifically mentioned in the Treaty of Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-tromelin_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tromelin-15">[13]</a></sup> Mauritius remained a primarily plantation-based colony of the United Kingdom until independence in 1968. </p>
      <p>In 1965, three years before Mauritius became independent, the UK split off the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a> from Mauritian territory, and also split off the islands of Aldabra, Farquhar, and Desroches from the Seychelles, to form the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> (BIOT).<sup id="cite_ref-Annex_11_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annex_11-16">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Chagossians" title="Expulsion of the Chagossians">local population was forcibly expelled</a> and the largest island, <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a>, was leased to the United States. The UK has restricted access to the Chagos Archipelago, allowing entry to casual tourists, the media, and former inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-visit_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visit-17">[15]</a></sup> The sovereignty of the Chagos is <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago_sovereignty_dispute" title="Chagos Archipelago sovereignty dispute">disputed</a> between Mauritius and the UK. In February 2019, the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> issued an advisory opinion ordering the UK to return the Chagos Islands to Mauritius as rapidly as possible to complete the decolonisation of Mauritius. </p>
      <p>Owing to its geographic location and centuries of colonialism, the <a href="/wiki/Mauritians" title="Mauritians">people of Mauritius</a> are highly diverse in ethnicity, <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">culture</a>, language and faith. It is the only country in Africa where <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the religion withe the most adherents.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> The island's government is closely modelled on the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_parliamentary_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Westminster parliamentary system">Westminster parliamentary system</a>, and Mauritius is highly ranked for <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">democracy</a> and for <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_freedom" title="List of countries by economic freedom">economic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom in the world">political freedom</a>. Mauritius is categorised as "very high" in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the country is classified as a <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WB_GROUP_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB_GROUP-20">[18]</a></sup> Mauritius is also ranked as the most competitive - and one of the most developed - economies in the African region.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> The country is a <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democracy</a>: The government provides free <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>; <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education</a> up through the tertiary level; and free public transportation for students, senior citizens, and the disabled.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-22">[20]</a></sup> In 2019, Mauritius was ranked the most peaceful African country by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Along with the other Mascarene Islands, Mauritius is known for its <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Mauritius" title="Wildlife of Mauritius">varied flora and fauna</a>. Many species are endemic to the island. The island was the only known home of the <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a>, which, along with several other avian species, was made extinct by human activities relatively soon after the island's settlement. </p>

         <ul>

          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Rodrigues_Island"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rodrigues Island</span></a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The first historical evidence of the existence of an island now known as Mauritius is on a map produced by the <a href="/wiki/Italian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian people">Italian</a> <a href="/wiki/Cartographer" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartographer">cartographer</a> Alberto Cantino in 1502.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> From this, it appears that Mauritius bore the name <i>Dina Arobi</i>, very likely the name shared with the Portuguese by sailors from the subcontinent. In 1507, Portuguese sailors visited the uninhabited island. The island appears with a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> name <i>Cirne</i> on early Portuguese maps, probably from the name of a ship in the 1507 expedition. Another Portuguese sailor, <a href="/wiki/Dom_(title)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dom (title)">Dom</a> <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mascarenhas" title="Pedro Mascarenhas">Pedro Mascarenhas</a>, gave the name <i><a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarenes</a></i> to the Archipelago. </p>
      <p>In 1598, Dutch squadron under Admiral Wybrand van Warwyck landed at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Port">Grand Port</a> and named the island <i>Mauritius</i>, in honour of <a href="/wiki/Maurice,_Prince_of_Orange" title="Maurice, Prince of Orange">Prince Maurice van Nassau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stadtholder" title="Stadtholder">stadtholder</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>. Later the island became a French colony and was renamed <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a>. On 3 December 1810, the French surrendered the island to Great Britain during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. Under British rule, the island's name reverted to <i>Mauritius</i> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Mauritius.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/En-us-Mauritius.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Mauritius.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>. Mauritius is also commonly known as <i>Maurice</i> (<small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[mɔˈʁis]</a></span>) and <i>Île Maurice</i> in French, <i>Moris</i> (<small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Mauritian_Creole" title="Help:IPA/Mauritian Creole">[moʁis]</a></span>) in <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole" title="Mauritian Creole">Mauritian Creole</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mauritius" title="History of Mauritius">History of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The island of Mauritius was uninhabited before its first recorded visit by Portuguese sailors in the beginning of the 16th century. The name Dina Arobi has been associated with Arab sailors. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_Mauritius">Portuguese Mauritius</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Portuguese Mauritius">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:D._Pedro_Mascarenhas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/D._Pedro_Mascarenhas.jpg/170px-D._Pedro_Mascarenhas.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="292" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/D._Pedro_Mascarenhas.jpg/255px-D._Pedro_Mascarenhas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/D._Pedro_Mascarenhas.jpg/340px-D._Pedro_Mascarenhas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="425" data-file-height="731"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:D._Pedro_Mascarenhas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mascarenhas" title="Pedro Mascarenhas">Pedro Mascarenhas</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">Viceroy of Portuguese India</a> and namesake of the <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarene Islands</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a> purported to give <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> the right to colonise this part of world. In 1507, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> sailors came to the uninhabited island and established a visiting base. <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Fernandes_Pereira" title="Diogo Fernandes Pereira">Diogo Fernandes Pereira</a>, a Portuguese navigator, was the first European known to land in Mauritius. He named the island "Ilha do Cirne" ("Island of Cirne"). The Portuguese did not stay long as they were not interested in these islands.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-27">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarene Islands</a> were named after <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mascarenhas" title="Pedro Mascarenhas">Pedro Mascarenhas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_Portuguese_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Viceroy of Portuguese India">Viceroy of Portuguese India</a>, after his visit to the islands in 1512. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rodrigues_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodrigues (island)">Rodrigues Island</a> was named after <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese explorer</a> <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Rodrigues" title="Diogo Rodrigues">Diogo Rodrigues</a>, who first came upon the island in 1528. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Dutch_Mauritius_.281638.E2.80.931710.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_Mauritius_(1638–1710)">Dutch Mauritius (1638–1710)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Dutch Mauritius (1638–1710)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Mauritius" title="Dutch Mauritius">Dutch Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Het_Tweede_Boeck.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Het_Tweede_Boeck.jpg/220px-Het_Tweede_Boeck.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Het_Tweede_Boeck.jpg/330px-Het_Tweede_Boeck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Het_Tweede_Boeck.jpg/440px-Het_Tweede_Boeck.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1525" data-file-height="1023"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Het_Tweede_Boeck.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dutch activities on the shore of Mauritius, as well as the first published depiction of a <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a> bird, on the left, 1601
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1598 a Dutch squadron under Admiral Wybrand Van Warwyck landed at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Port">Grand Port</a> and named the island "Mauritius" after <a href="/wiki/Maurice,_Prince_of_Orange" title="Maurice, Prince of Orange">Prince Maurice of Nassau</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i>Maurits van Nassau</i>) of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>. The Dutch inhabited the island in 1638, from which they exploited <a href="/wiki/Ebony" title="Ebony">ebony</a> trees and introduced <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domestic_animals" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic animals">domestic animals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>. It was from here that Dutch navigator <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> set out to seek the Great Southern Land, mapping parts of <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aotearoa" title="Aotearoa">Aotearoa</a>/New Zealand and <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>. The first Dutch settlement lasted 20 years. In 1639 slaves arrived in Mauritius from Madagascar. The Dutch East India Company brought them to cut down ebony trees and to work in the new tobacco and sugar cane plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-The_slave_trade_on_Mauritius_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_slave_trade_on_Mauritius-28">[26]</a></sup> Several attempts to establish a colony permanently were subsequently made, but the settlements never developed enough to produce dividends, causing the Dutch to abandon Mauritius in 1710.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-27">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="French_Mauritius_.281715.E2.80.931810.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Mauritius_(1715–1810)">French Mauritius (1715–1810)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: French Mauritius (1715–1810)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France (Mauritius)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>France, which already controlled neighbouring Île Bourbon (now <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a>), took control of Mauritius in 1715 and renamed it <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a>. In 1723, the <a href="/wiki/Code_Noir" title="Code Noir">Code Noir</a> was established to categorise one group of human beings as "goods", in order for the owner of these goods to be able to obtain insurance money and compensation in case of loss of his "goods".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> The 1735 arrival of French governor <a href="/wiki/Bertrand-Fran%C3%A7ois_Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais" title="Bertrand-François Mahé de La Bourdonnais">Bertrand-François Mahé de La Bourdonnais</a> coincided with development of a prosperous economy based on sugar production. Mahé de La Bourdonnais established <a href="/wiki/Port_Louis" title="Port Louis">Port Louis</a> as a naval base and a shipbuilding centre.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-27">[25]</a></sup> Under his governorship, numerous buildings were erected, a number of which are still standing. These include part of Government House, the Château de Mon Plaisir, and the Line Barracks, the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Police_Force" title="Mauritius Police Force">police force</a>. The island was under the administration of the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a>, which maintained its presence until 1767.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-27">[25]</a></sup> During the French rule slaves were brought from parts of Africa such as Mozambique and Zanzibar.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> As a result the island's population rose dramatically from 15,000 to 49,000 within 30 thirty years. During the late eighteenth century African slaves accounted for around 80 percent of the island’s population, and by the early nineteenth century there were 60,000 slaves on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-The_slave_trade_on_Mauritius_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_slave_trade_on_Mauritius-28">[26]</a></sup> In early 1729 Indians from <a href="/wiki/Pondicherry" title="Pondicherry">Pondicherry, India</a> arrived in Mauritius aboard the vessel <i>La Sirène</i>. Work contracts for these craftsmen were signed in 1734 at the time when they acquired their freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg/220px-Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg/330px-Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg/440px-Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3465" data-file-height="2192"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grand_Port" title="Battle of Grand Port">Battle of Grand Port</a> between French and British naval forces, 20–27 August 1810
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>From 1767 to 1810, except for a brief period during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> when the inhabitants set up a government virtually independent of France, the island was controlled by officials appointed by the French government. <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Henri_Bernardin_de_Saint-Pierre" title="Jacques-Henri Bernardin de Saint-Pierre">Jacques-Henri Bernardin de Saint-Pierre</a> lived on the island from 1768 to 1771, then went back to France, where he wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Paul_et_Virginie" title="Paul et Virginie">Paul et Virginie</a></i>, a love story that made the Isle de France famous wherever the French language was spoken. In 1796 the settlers broke away from French control when the government in Paris attempted to abolish slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> Two famous French governors were the Vicomte de Souillac (who constructed the Chaussée in Port Louis<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint2_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint2-34">[32]</a></sup> and encouraged farmers to settle in the district of Savanne) and <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Bruni_d%27Entrecasteaux" title="Antoine Bruni d'Entrecasteaux">Antoine Bruni d'Entrecasteaux</a> (who saw to it that the French in the Indian Ocean should have their headquarters in Mauritius instead of <a href="/wiki/Pondicherry" title="Pondicherry">Pondicherry</a> in India).<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-35">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Mathieu_Isidore_Decaen" title="Charles Mathieu Isidore Decaen">Charles Mathieu Isidore Decaen</a> was a successful general in the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a> and, in some ways, a rival of <a href="/wiki/Napol%C3%A9on_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoléon I">Napoléon I</a>. He ruled as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Governor of Isle de France (Mauritius)">Governor of Isle de France</a> and Réunion from 1803 to 1810. British naval <a href="/wiki/Cartographer" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartographer">cartographer</a> and explorer <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Flinders" title="Matthew Flinders">Matthew Flinders</a> was arrested and detained by General Decaen on the island from 1803 to 1810,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> in contravention of an order from Napoléon. During the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Mauritius became a base from which <a href="/wiki/French_corsairs" title="French corsairs">French corsairs</a> organised successful raids on British commercial ships. The raids continued until 1810, when a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> expedition led by <a href="/wiki/Commodore_(Royal_Navy)" title="Commodore (Royal Navy)">Commodore</a> <a href="/wiki/Josias_Rowley" title="Josias Rowley">Josias Rowley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">R.N.</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Irish">Anglo-Irish</a> <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy_(class)" title="Aristocracy (class)">aristocrat</a>, was sent to capture the island. Despite winning the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grand_Port" title="Battle of Grand Port">Battle of Grand Port</a>, the only French naval victory over the British during these wars, the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_%C3%8Ele_de_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Île de France">French could not prevent the British from landing</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cap_Malheureux" title="Cap Malheureux">Cap Malheureux</a> three months later. They formally surrendered the island on the fifth day of the invasion, 3 December 1810,<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-35">[33]</a></sup> on terms allowing settlers to keep their land and property and to use the French language and law of France in criminal and civil matters. Under British rule, the island's name reverted to Mauritius.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-27">[25]</a></sup> The swift conquest of Mauritius was fictionalised in the novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mauritius_Command" title="The Mauritius Command">The Mauritius Command</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_O%27Brian" title="Patrick O'Brian">Patrick O'Brian</a>, first published in 1977. </p> 
      <h3><span id="British_Mauritius_.281810.E2.80.931968.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Mauritius_(1810–1968)">British Mauritius (1810–1968)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: British Mauritius (1810–1968)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Mauritius" title="British Mauritius">British Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Isle_of_France,_2_December_1810.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Isle_of_France%2C_2_December_1810.jpg/220px-Isle_of_France%2C_2_December_1810.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Isle_of_France%2C_2_December_1810.jpg/330px-Isle_of_France%2C_2_December_1810.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Isle_of_France%2C_2_December_1810.jpg/440px-Isle_of_France%2C_2_December_1810.jpg 2x" data-file-width="860" data-file-height="626"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Isle_of_France,_2_December_1810.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>British forces <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Isle_de_France" title="Invasion of Isle de France">seizing the Isle of France</a> on 2 December 1810
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The British administration, which began with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Townsend_Farquhar" title="Robert Townsend Farquhar">Sir Robert Farquhar</a> as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_British_Mauritius" title="Governor of British Mauritius">governor</a>, led to rapid social and economic changes. However, it was tainted by the Ratsitatane episode. Ratsitatane, nephew of King Radama of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, was brought to Mauritius as a political prisoner. He managed to escape from prison and plotted a rebellion that would free the island's slaves. He was betrayed by an associate and was caught by the British forces, summarily judged, and condemned to death. He was beheaded at Plaine Verte on 15 April 1822, and his head was displayed as a deterrent against future uprisings among the slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Selvon_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Selvon-38">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1832, Adrien d'Épinay launched the first Mauritian newspaper (<i>Le Cernéen</i>), which was not controlled by the government. In the same year, there was a move by the procureur-general to abolish slavery without compensation to the slave owners. This gave rise to discontent, and, to check an eventual rebellion, the government ordered all the inhabitants to surrender their arms. Furthermore, a stone fortress, Fort Adelaide, was built on a hill (now known as the Citadel hill) in the centre of Port Louis to quell any uprising.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint2_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint2-34">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> was abolished in 1835, and the planters ultimately received two million pounds sterling in compensation for the loss of their slaves, who had been imported from Africa and Madagascar during the French occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">abolition of slavery</a> had important impacts on Mauritius's society, economy and population. The planters brought a large number of <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured servant">indentured labourers</a> from India to work in the sugar cane fields. Between 1834 and 1921, around half a million indentured labourers were present on the island. They worked on sugar estates, factories, in transport and on construction sites. Additionally, the British brought 8,740 <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indian</a> soldiers to the island.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-27">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aapravasi_Ghat" title="Aapravasi Ghat">Aapravasi Ghat</a>, in the bay at <a href="/wiki/Port_Louis" title="Port Louis">Port Louis</a> and now a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> site, was the first British <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a> to serve as a major reception centre for <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servants" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured servants">indentured servants</a>. </p>
      <p>An important figure of the 19th century was Rémy Ollier, a journalist of mixed origin. In 1828, the colour bar was officially abolished in Mauritius, but British governors gave little power to coloured persons, and appointed only whites as leading officials. Rémy Ollier petitioned to <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> to allow coloureds in the council of government, and this became possible a few years later. He also made Port Louis become a municipality so that the citizens could administer the town through their own elected representatives. A street has been named after him in Port Louis, and his bust was erected in the Jardin de la Compagnie in 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-35">[33]</a></sup> In 1885 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mauritius_(1885)" title="Constitution of Mauritius (1885)">a new constitution</a> was introduced and it was referred to a <i>Cens Démocratique</i> as it incorporated some of the principles advocated by one of the Creole leaders called Onesipho Beaugeard. It created elected positions in the Legislative Council although the franchise was restricted mainly to the white French and fair-skinned Creole elite who owned real estate. In 1886 Governor <a href="/wiki/John_Pope_Hennessy" title="John Pope Hennessy">John Pope Hennessy</a> nominated Gnanadicarayen Arlanda as the first ever <a href="/wiki/Indo-Mauritian" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Mauritian">Indo-Mauritian</a> member of the ruling Council despite the sugar oligarchy's preference for rival Indo-Mauritian Emile Sandapa. Arlanda served until 1891.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> Two main political parties were active at that time, the pro-Hennessy party being Sir William Newton's Reform Party where as the anti-Hennessy party Democrats was led by Gustave de Coriolis and Onésipho Beaugeard.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg/220px-Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg/330px-Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg/440px-Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="708"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse" title="Champ de Mars Racecourse">Champ de Mars Racecourse</a>, Port Louis, 1880
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The labourers brought from India were not always fairly treated, and a German, Adolph von Plevitz, made himself the unofficial protector of these immigrants. He mixed with many of the labourers, and in 1871 helped them to write a petition that was sent to <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Hamilton-Gordon,_1st_Baron_Stanmore" title="Arthur Hamilton-Gordon, 1st Baron Stanmore">Governor Gordon</a>. A commission was appointed to look into the complaints made by the Indian immigrants, and in 1872 two lawyers, appointed by the British Crown, were sent from England to make an inquiry. This Royal Commission recommended several measures that would affect the lives of Indian labourers during the next fifty years.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-35">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 1901, <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a> visited Mauritius, on his way from South Africa to India. He stayed on the island for two weeks, and urged the Indo-Mauritian community to take an interest in education and to play a more active role in politics. Back in India, he sent over a young lawyer, <a href="/wiki/Manilal_Doctor" title="Manilal Doctor">Manilal Doctor</a>, to improve the plight of the Indo-Mauritians. During the same year, faster links were established with the island of Rodrigues thanks to the wireless.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-42">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1903, motorcars were introduced in Mauritius, and in 1910 the first taxis, operated by Joseph Merven, came into service. The electrification of Port Louis took place in 1909, and in the same decade the Mauritius Hydro Electric Company of the <a href="/wiki/Amode_Ibrahim_Atchia" title="Amode Ibrahim Atchia">Atchia Brothers</a> was authorised to provide power to the towns of upper Plaines Wilhems. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_web_of_empire_-_a_diary_of_the_imperial_tour_of_their_Royal_Highnesses_the_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cornwall_and_York_in_1901_(1902)_(14763807672).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_web_of_empire_-_a_diary_of_the_imperial_tour_of_their_Royal_Highnesses_the_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cornwall_and_York_in_1901_%281902%29_%2814763807672%29.jpg/220px-The_web_of_empire_-_a_diary_of_the_imperial_tour_of_their_Royal_Highnesses_the_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cornwall_and_York_in_1901_%281902%29_%2814763807672%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_web_of_empire_-_a_diary_of_the_imperial_tour_of_their_Royal_Highnesses_the_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cornwall_and_York_in_1901_%281902%29_%2814763807672%29.jpg/330px-The_web_of_empire_-_a_diary_of_the_imperial_tour_of_their_Royal_Highnesses_the_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cornwall_and_York_in_1901_%281902%29_%2814763807672%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_web_of_empire_-_a_diary_of_the_imperial_tour_of_their_Royal_Highnesses_the_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cornwall_and_York_in_1901_%281902%29_%2814763807672%29.jpg/440px-The_web_of_empire_-_a_diary_of_the_imperial_tour_of_their_Royal_Highnesses_the_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cornwall_and_York_in_1901_%281902%29_%2814763807672%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1718"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_web_of_empire_-_a_diary_of_the_imperial_tour_of_their_Royal_Highnesses_the_Duke_and_Duchess_of_Cornwall_and_York_in_1901_(1902)_(14763807672).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Duke and Duchess of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cornwall" title="Duchy of Cornwall">Cornwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_York" title="Duke of York">York</a> in Mauritius, 1901
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The 1910s were a period of political agitation. The rising middle class (made up of doctors, lawyers, and teachers) began to challenge the political power of the sugar cane landowners. Dr. Eugène Laurent, mayor of Port Louis, was the leader of this new group; his party, Action Libérale, demanded that more people should be allowed to vote in the elections. Action Libérale was opposed by the Parti de l'Ordre, led by Henri Leclézio, the most influential of the sugar magnates.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_35-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-35">[33]</a></sup> In 1911 there were riots in Port Louis due to a false rumour that Dr. Eugène Laurent had been murdered by the oligarchs in Curepipe. This became known as the <a href="/wiki/1911_Curepipe_riots" title="1911 Curepipe riots">1911 Curepipe riots</a>. Shops and offices were damaged in the capital, and one person was killed. In the same year, 1911, the first public cinema shows took place in Curepipe, and, in the same town, a stone building was erected to house the Royal College.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-42">[40]</a></sup> In 1912, a wider telephone network came into service, used by the government, business firms, and a few private households. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> broke out in August 1914. Many Mauritians volunteered to fight in Europe against the Germans and in <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> against the Turks. But the war affected Mauritius much less than the wars of the eighteenth century. In fact, the 1914–1918 war was a period of great prosperity due to a boom in sugar prices. In 1919 the Mauritius Sugar Syndicate came into being, which included 70% of all sugar producers.<sup id="cite_ref-Republic_of_Mauritius-_History_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Republic_of_Mauritius-_History-43">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 1920s saw the rise of a "retrocessionism" movement, which favoured the retrocession of Mauritius to France. The movement rapidly collapsed because none of the candidates who wanted Mauritius to be given back to France were elected in the 1921 elections. In the post-war recession, there was a sharp drop in sugar prices. Many sugar estates closed down, marking the end of an era for the sugar magnates who had not only controlled the economy but also the political life of the country. Raoul Rivet, the editor of <i>Le Mauricien</i> newspaper, campaigned for a revision of the constitution that would give the emerging middle class a greater role in the running of the country. The principles of <a href="/wiki/Arya_Samaj" title="Arya Samaj">Arya Samaj</a> began to infiltrate the Hindu community, who clamoured for more social justice.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-42">[40]</a></sup> At the 1926 elections Dunputh Lallah and Rajcoomar Gujadhur became the first <a href="/wiki/Indo-Mauritians" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Mauritians">Indo-Mauritians</a> to be elected at the Legislative Council. At Grand Port Lallah won over rivals Fernand Louis Morel and Gaston Gebert; at Flacq Gujadhur defeated Pierre Montocchio. After the end of nominated Arlanda's term in 1891 and until 1926 there had been no Indo-Mauritian representation in the Legislative Council.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>1936 saw the birth of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Mauritius)" title="Labour Party (Mauritius)">Labour Party</a>, launched by Dr. <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Cur%C3%A9" title="Maurice Curé">Maurice Curé</a>. <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Anquetil" title="Emmanuel Anquetil">Emmanuel Anquetil</a> rallied the urban workers while Pandit Sahadeo concentrated on the rural working class.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Uba_riots_of_1937" title="Uba riots of 1937">Uba riots of 1937</a> resulted in reforms by the local British government that improved labour conditions and led to the un-banning of labour unions.<sup id="cite_ref-js_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-js-46">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rg_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-47">[45]</a></sup> Labour Day was celebrated for the first time in 1938. More than 30,000 workers sacrificed a day's wage and came from all over the island to attend a giant meeting at the Champ de Mars.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> Following the dockers' strikes trade unionist <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Anquetil" title="Emmanuel Anquetil">Emmanuel Anquetil</a> was deported to Rodrigues, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Cur%C3%A9" title="Maurice Curé">Maurice Curé</a> and Pandit Sahadeo were placed under house arrest whilst numerous strikers were jailed. Governor Sir <a href="/wiki/Bede_Clifford" title="Bede Clifford">Bede Clifford</a> assisted Mr Jules Leclezio of the Mauritius Sugar Syndicate to counter the effects of the strike by using alternative workers known as ‘black legs’.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in 1939, many Mauritians volunteered to serve under the British flag in Africa and the Near East, fighting against the German and Italian armies. Some went to England to become pilots and ground staff in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>. Mauritius was never really threatened but several British ships were sunk outside Port Louis by German submarines in 1943. </p>
      <p>During World War II, conditions were hard in the country; the prices of commodities doubled but workers’ salaries increased only by 10 to 20 percent. There was civil unrest, and the colonial government censored all trade union activities. However, the labourers of Belle Vue Harel Sugar Estate went on strike on 27 September 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> Police officers eventually fired directly at the crowd, resulting in the deaths of 4 labourers Soondrum Pavatdan (better known as Anjalay Coopen the 32 year old pregnant woman), Moonsamy Moonien (14 year old boy), Kistnasamy Mooneesamy (37 year old labourer), and Marday Panapen.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> This became known as the <a href="/wiki/Belle_Vue_Harel_Massacre" title="Belle Vue Harel Massacre">Belle Vue Harel Massacre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> Social worker and leader of the Jan Andolan movement <a href="/wiki/Basdeo_Bissoondoyal" title="Basdeo Bissoondoyal">Basdeo Bissoondoyal</a> organised the funeral ceremonies of the 4 dead labourers.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> Three months later <a href="/wiki/Basdeo_Bissoondoyal" title="Basdeo Bissoondoyal">Basdeo Bissoondoyal</a> organised a mass gathering at "Marie Reine de la Paix" in Port Louis on 12 December 1943 and the significant crowd of workers from all over the island confirmed the popularity of his movement Jan Andolan.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the proclamation of the new <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.eisa.org.za/wep/mauoverview7.htm">1947 Constitution</a> the general elections were held on 9 August 1948 and for the first time the colonial government expanded the franchise to all adults who could write their name in one of the island's 19 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-CD_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CD-56">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Guy_Rozemont" title="Guy Rozemont">Guy Rozemont</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Mauritius)" title="Labour Party (Mauritius)">Labour Party</a> won the majority of the votes<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> with 11 of the 19 elected seats won by <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a>. However, the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_British_Mauritius" title="Governor of British Mauritius">Governor-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Mackenzie-Kennedy" title="Donald Mackenzie-Kennedy">Donald Mackenzie-Kennedy</a> appointed 12 Conservatives to the Legislative Council on 23 August 1948 to perpetuate the predominance of white <a href="/wiki/Franco-Mauritians" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Mauritians">Franco-Mauritians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CD_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CD-56">[54]</a></sup> In 1948 <a href="/wiki/Emilienne_Rochecouste" title="Emilienne Rochecouste">Emilienne Rochecouste</a> became the first woman to be elected to the Legislative Council, serving until 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-RR_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RR-59">[57]</a></sup> Guy Rozemont's party bettered its position in 1953, and, on the strength of the election results, demanded <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a>. Constitutional conferences were held in London in 1955 and 1957, and the ministerial system was introduced. Voting took place for the first time on the basis of universal adult suffrage on 9 March 1959. The general election was again won by the Labour Party, led this time by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam">Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ram_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ram-60">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A Constitutional Review Conference was held in London in 1961, and a programme of further constitutional advance was established. The 1963 election was won by the Labour Party and its allies. The <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Office" title="Colonial Office">Colonial Office</a> noted that politics of a communal nature was gaining ground in Mauritius and that the choice of candidates (by parties) and the voting behaviour (of electors) were governed by ethnic and caste considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-ram_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ram-60">[58]</a></sup> Around that time, two eminent British academics, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Titmuss" title="Richard Titmuss">Richard Titmuss</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Meade" title="James Meade">James Meade</a>, published a report of the island's social problems caused by overpopulation and the monoculture of sugar cane. This led to an intense campaign to halt the population explosion, and the decade registered a sharp decline in population growth. </p>
      <p>In early 1965 a political assassination took place in the suburb of Belle-Rose in the town of Quatre Bornes when Labour activist Rampersad Surath was beaten to death by thugs of rival party Parti Mauricien.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> On 10 May 1965 <a href="/wiki/1965_Mauritius_race_riots" title="1965 Mauritius race riots">racial riots</a> broke out in the village of <i>Trois Boutiques</i> near <a href="/wiki/Souillac,_Mauritius" title="Souillac, Mauritius">Souillac</a> and progressed to the historic village of <a href="/wiki/Mahebourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahebourg">Mahebourg</a>. A nationwide State of Emergency was declared on the British colony. The riot was initiated by the murder of Police Constable Beesoo in his vehicle by a Creole gang. This was followed by the murder of a civilian named Mr. Robert Brousse in Trois Boutiques.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> The Creole gang then proceeded to the coastal historic village of Mahebourg to assault the Indo-Mauritian spectators who were watching a Hindustani movie at Cinéma Odéon. Mahebourg police recorded nearly 100 complaints of assaults on Indo-Mauritians.<sup id="cite_ref-vm_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vm-64">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.28since_1968.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(since_1968)">Independence (since 1968)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Independence (since 1968)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_(1968%E2%80%931992)" title="Mauritius (1968–1992)">Mauritius (1968–1992)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>At the Lancaster Conference of 1965, it became clear that Britain wanted to relieve itself of the colony of Mauritius. In 1959, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a> had made his famous <i><a href="/wiki/Wind_of_Change_(speech)" title="Wind of Change (speech)">Winds of Change Speech</a></i> where he acknowledged that the best option for Britain was to give complete independence to its colonies. Thus, since the late Fifties, the way was paved for independence.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Later in 1965, after the Lancaster Conference, the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a> was excised from the territory of Mauritius to form the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> (BIOT). A general election took place on 7 August 1967, and the <a href="/wiki/Independence_Party_(Mauritius)" title="Independence Party (Mauritius)">Independence Party</a> obtained the majority of seats. In January 1968, six weeks before the declaration of independence the <a href="/wiki/1968_Mauritian_riots" title="1968 Mauritian riots">1968 Mauritian riots</a> occurred in Port Louis leading to the deaths of 25 people.<sup id="cite_ref-mg_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mg-66">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eisa_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eisa-67">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg/190px-Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg/285px-Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg/380px-Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="664"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> was <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Mauritius" title="Queen of Mauritius">Queen of Mauritius</a> from 1968 to 1992.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mauritius adopted a new constitution and independence was proclaimed on 12 March 1968. Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam became the first prime minister of an independent Mauritius with Queen Elizabeth II remaining head of state as Queen of Mauritius. In 1969, the opposition party <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Militant_Movement" title="Mauritian Militant Movement">Mauritian Militant Movement</a> (MMM) led by <a href="/wiki/Paul_B%C3%A9renger" title="Paul Bérenger">Paul Bérenger</a> was founded. Later in 1971, the MMM, backed by unions, called a series of strikes in the port, which caused a state of emergency in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> The coalition government of the Labour Party and the PMSD (Parti Mauricien Social Démocrate) reacted by curtailing civil liberties and curbing freedom of the press.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-42">[40]</a></sup> Two unsuccessful assassination attempts were made against Paul Bérenger. On 1 October 1971 his supporter Fareed Muttur died in suspicious circumstances at Le Réduit whilst driving Paul Bérenger's car.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> The second led to the death of <a href="/wiki/Azor_Adelaide" title="Azor Adelaide">Azor Adélaïde</a>, a dock worker and activist, on 25 November 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> General elections were postponed and public meetings were prohibited. Members of the MMM including Paul Bérenger were imprisoned on 23 December 1971. The MMM leader was released a year later.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 1975, a student revolt that started at the University of Mauritius swept across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> The students were unsatisfied with an education system that did not meet their aspirations and gave limited prospects for future employment. On 20 May, thousands of students tried to enter Port-Louis over the Grand River North West bridge and clashed with police. An act of Parliament was passed on 16 December 1975 to extend the right to vote to 18-year-olds. This was seen as an attempt to appease the frustration of the younger generation.<sup id="cite_ref-Selvon_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Selvon-38">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The next general elections took place on <a href="/wiki/1976_Mauritian_general_election" title="1976 Mauritian general election">20 December 1976</a>. The Labour-CAM coalition won only 28 seats out of 62.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> The MMM secured 34 seats in Parliament but outgoing Prime Minister Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam managed to remain in office, with a two-seat majority, after striking an alliance with the PMSD of Gaetan Duval. </p>
      <p>In 1982 an <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Militant_Movement" title="Mauritian Militant Movement">MMM</a>-<a href="/wiki/Parti_Socialiste_Mauricien" title="Parti Socialiste Mauricien">PSM</a> government (led by <a href="/wiki/List_of_prime_ministers_of_Mauritius" title="List of prime ministers of Mauritius">PM</a> <a href="/wiki/Anerood_Jugnauth" title="Anerood Jugnauth">Anerood Jugnauth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius" title="Deputy Prime Minister of Mauritius">Deputy PM</a> <a href="/wiki/Harish_Boodhoo" title="Harish Boodhoo">Harish Boodhoo</a> and Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Paul_B%C3%A9renger" title="Paul Bérenger">Paul Bérenger</a>) was elected. However, ideological and personality differences emerged within the MMM and PSM leadership. The power struggle between Bérenger and Jugnauth peaked in March 1983. Jugnauth travelled to New Delhi to attend a <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> summit; on his return, Bérenger proposed constitutional changes that would strip power from the Prime Minister. At Jugnauth's request, PM <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a> of India planned an armed intervention involving the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Navy" title="Indian Navy">Indian Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">Indian Army</a> to prevent a <a href="/wiki/Coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Coup">coup</a> under the code name <a href="/wiki/Operation_Lal_Dora" title="Operation Lal Dora">Operation Lal Dora</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Militant_Movement" title="Mauritian Militant Movement">MMM</a>-<a href="/wiki/Parti_Socialiste_Mauricien" title="Parti Socialiste Mauricien">PSM</a> government split up nine months after the June 1982 election. According to an Information Ministry official the nine months was a "socialist experiment".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Harish_Boodhoo" title="Harish Boodhoo">Harish Boodhoo</a> dissolved his party <a href="/wiki/Parti_Socialiste_Mauricien" title="Parti Socialiste Mauricien">PSM</a> to enable all PSM parliamentarians to join Jugnauth's new party MSM, thus remaining in power whilst distancing themselves from <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Militant_Movement" title="Mauritian Militant Movement">MMM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> The MSM-Labour-PMSD coalition was victorious at the <a href="/wiki/1983_Mauritian_general_election" title="1983 Mauritian general election">August 1983</a> elections, resulting in <a href="/wiki/Anerood_Jugnauth" title="Anerood Jugnauth">Anerood Jugnauth</a> as PM and <a href="/wiki/Ga%C3%ABtan_Duval" title="Gaëtan Duval">Gaëtan Duval</a> as <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius" title="Deputy Prime Minister of Mauritius">Deputy PM</a>. </p>
      <p>That period saw growth in the EPZ (Export Processing Zone) sector. Industrialisation began to spread to villages as well, and attracted young workers from all ethnic communities. As a result, the sugar industry began to lose its hold on the economy. Large retail chains began opening stores in 1985 and offered credit facilities to low-income earners, thus allowing them to afford basic household appliances. There was also a boom in the tourism industry, and new hotels sprang up throughout the island. In 1989 the stock exchange opened its doors and in 1992 the freeport began operation.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_42-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-42">[40]</a></sup> In 1990, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_prime_ministers_of_Mauritius" title="List of prime ministers of Mauritius">Prime Minister</a> lost the vote on changing the Constitution to make the country a republic with Bérenger as President.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Republic_.28since_1992.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_(since_1992)">Republic (since 1992)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Republic (since 1992)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 12 March 1992, twenty-four years after independence, Mauritius was proclaimed a republic within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_27-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-27">[25]</a></sup> The last governor general, <a href="/wiki/Veerasamy_Ringadoo" title="Veerasamy Ringadoo">Sir Veerasamy Ringadoo</a>, became the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mauritius" title="President of Mauritius">president</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> This was under a transitional arrangement, in which he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Cassam_Uteem" title="Cassam Uteem">Cassam Uteem</a> later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> Political power remained with the prime minister. </p>
      <p>Despite an improvement in the economy, which coincided with a fall in the price of petrol and a favourable dollar exchange rate, the government did not enjoy full popularity. As early as 1984, there was discontent. Through the <i>Newspapers and Periodicals Amendment Act</i>, the government tried to make every newspaper provide a bank guarantee of half a million rupees. Forty-three journalists protested by participating in a public demonstration in Port Louis, in front of Parliament. They were arrested and freed on bail. This caused a public outcry and the government had to review its policy.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_42-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-42">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There was also dissatisfaction in the education sector. There were not enough high-quality secondary colleges to answer the growing demand of primary school leavers who had got through their CPE (Certificate of Primary Education). In 1991, a master plan for education failed to get national support and contributed to the government's downfall.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_42-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-42">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 1995 <a href="/wiki/Navin_Ramgoolam" title="Navin Ramgoolam">Navin Ramgoolam</a> was elected as <a href="/wiki/List_of_prime_ministers_of_Mauritius" title="List of prime ministers of Mauritius">PM</a> of the Labour-MMM alliance. In October 1996 the triple murder of political activists at Gorah-Issac Street in Port Louis led to several arrests and a long investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> The year 1999 was marked by civil unrest and riots in <a href="/wiki/1999_Mauritian_riots" title="1999 Mauritian riots">February</a> and then in <a href="/wiki/1999_L%27Amicale_riots" title="1999 L'Amicale riots">May</a>. Following the Kaya riots President <a href="/wiki/Cassam_Uteem" title="Cassam Uteem">Cassam Uteem</a> and Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Jean_Marg%C3%A9ot" title="Jean Margéot">Jean Margéot</a> toured the country and calm was restored after four days of turmoil.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> A commission of enquiry was set up to investigate the root causes of the social disturbance. The resulting report delved into the cause of poverty and qualified many tenacious beliefs as perceptions.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> In January 2000 political activist Rajen Sabapathee was shot dead after he escaped from La Bastille jail.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mauriceybbrfrinwodas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Mauriceybbrfrinwodas.jpg/220px-Mauriceybbrfrinwodas.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Mauriceybbrfrinwodas.jpg/330px-Mauriceybbrfrinwodas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Mauriceybbrfrinwodas.jpg/440px-Mauriceybbrfrinwodas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mauriceybbrfrinwodas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Perceived failure of <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Mauritius" title="Government of Mauritius">the government</a> to respond promptly and effectively to the <a href="/wiki/MV_Wakashio_oil_spill" title="MV Wakashio oil spill">MV <i>Wakashio</i> oil spill</a> has resulted in anti-government protests.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Anerood Jugnauth of the MSM returned to power in September 2000 after securing an alliance with the MMM. In 2002, the island of <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a> became an autonomous entity within the republic and was thus able to elect its own representatives to administer the island. In 2003, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_prime_ministers_of_Mauritius" title="List of prime ministers of Mauritius">prime ministership</a> was transferred to Paul Bérenger of the MMM, and Anerood Jugnauth became president. Bérenger was the first Franco-Mauritian Prime Minister in the country's post-Independence history. </p>
      <p>In 2005, Navin Ramgoolam became PM under the new coalition of Labour-PMXD-VF-MR-MMSM. In 2010 the Labour-MSM-PMSD alliance secured power and Navin Ramgoolam remained PM until 2014. </p>
      <p>The MSM-PMSD-ML coalition was victorious at the 2014 elections under Anerood Jugnauth's leadership. Despite disagreements within the ruling alliance which led to the departure of PMSD, the MSM-ML stayed in power for their full 5-year term. </p>
      <p>On 21 January 2017 Anerood Jugnauth announced his resignation and that his son and Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Pravind_Jugnauth" title="Pravind Jugnauth">Pravind Jugnauth</a> would assume the office of prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> The transition took place as planned on 23 January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, Mauritian president <a href="/wiki/Ameenah_Gurib-Fakim" title="Ameenah Gurib-Fakim">Ameenah Gurib-Fakim</a> (the only former female head of state in the African Union) resigned over a financial scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> The incumbent president is <a href="/wiki/Prithvirajsing_Roopun" title="Prithvirajsing Roopun">Prithvirajsing Roopun</a><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> who has served since December 2019. </p>
      <p>On 25 July 2020, Japanese-owned bulk carrier MV Wakashio ran aground on a coral reef off the coast of Mauritius, leaking up to 1,000 tonnes of heavy oil into a pristine lagoon.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> Its location on the edge of protected fragile marine ecosystems and a wetland of international importance made the <a href="/wiki/MV_Wakashio_oil_spill" title="MV Wakashio oil spill"><i>MV Wakashio</i> oil spill</a> one of the worst <a href="/wiki/Environmental_disaster" title="Environmental disaster">environmental disasters</a> ever to hit the western Indian Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mauritius" title="Geography of Mauritius">Geography of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The total land area of the country is 2,040&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (790&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">170th largest nation</a> in the world by size. The Republic of Mauritius is constituted of Mauritius Island and <a href="/wiki/Outer_Islands_of_Mauritius" title="Outer Islands of Mauritius">several outlying islands</a>. The nation's <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a> (EEZ) covers about 2.3&nbsp;million&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (890,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of the Indian Ocean, including approximately 400,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (150,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) jointly managed with the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mauritius_Island">Mauritius Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Mauritius Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Mauritius is 2,000&nbsp;km (1,200&nbsp;mi) off the southeast coast of Africa, between latitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_south" title="19th parallel south">19°58.8'S</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_parallel_south" title="20th parallel south">20°31.7'S</a> and longitudes <a href="/wiki/57th_meridian_east" title="57th meridian east">57°18.0'E</a> and <a href="/wiki/57th_meridian_east" title="57th meridian east">57°46.5'E</a>. It is 65&nbsp;km (40&nbsp;mi) long and 45&nbsp;km (30&nbsp;mi) wide. Its land area is 1,864.8&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (720.0&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> The island is surrounded by more than 150&nbsp;km (100&nbsp;mi) of white sandy beaches, and the lagoons are protected from the open sea by the world's third-largest coral reef, which surrounds the island.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> Just off the Mauritian coast lie some 49 uninhabited islands and <a href="/wiki/Islets_of_Mauritius" title="Islets of Mauritius">islets</a>, several of which have been declared natural reserves for endangered species. </p>
      <p>The Mauritius Island (<a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole" title="Mauritian Creole">Mauritian Creole</a>: <i>Isle Moris</i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Île Maurice</i>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[il mɔʁis]</a></span>) is relatively young geologically, having been created by volcanic activity some 8 million years ago. Together with Saint Brandon, Réunion, and Rodrigues, the island is part of the <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarene Islands</a>. These islands emerged as a result of gigantic underwater volcanic eruptions that happened thousands of kilometres to the east of the continental block made up of Africa and Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-territory_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-territory-98">[96]</a></sup> They are no longer volcanically active and the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union_hotspot" title="Réunion hotspot">hotspot</a> now rests under Réunion Island. Mauritius is encircled by a broken ring of mountain ranges, varying in height from 300–800&nbsp;m (1,000–2,600&nbsp;ft) above sea level. The land rises from coastal plains to a central plateau where it reaches a height of 670&nbsp;m (2,200&nbsp;ft); the highest peak is in the south-west, <a href="/wiki/Piton_de_la_Petite_Rivi%C3%A8re_Noire" title="Piton de la Petite Rivière Noire">Piton de la Petite Rivière Noire</a> at 828 metres (2,717&nbsp;ft). Streams and rivers speckle the island, many formed in the cracks created by lava flows. </p> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:652px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Mauritius.png/650px-Mauritius.png" decoding="async" width="650" height="276" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Mauritius.png/975px-Mauritius.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Mauritius.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="435"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
