           <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>A panoramic view of Mauritius Island
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rodrigues_Island">Rodrigues Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rodrigues Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The autonomous island of <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a> is located 560&nbsp;km (350&nbsp;mi) to the east of Mauritius, with an area 108&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (42&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-territory_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-territory-98">[96]</a></sup> Rodrigues is a <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_island" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic island">volcanic island</a> rising from a ridge along the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Plateau" title="Mascarene Plateau">Mascarene Plateau</a>. The island is hilly with a central spine culminating in the highest peak, Mountain Limon at 398&nbsp;m (1,306&nbsp;ft). The island also has a <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reef</a> and extensive <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> deposits. According to Statistics Mauritius, at 1 July 2019, the population of the island was estimated at 43,371.<sup id="cite_ref-1_July_2019_Statistics_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1_July_2019_Statistics-99">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chagos_Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Chagos Archipelago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Chagos Archipelago is composed of atolls and islands, and is located approximately 2,200 kilometres north-east of the main island of Mauritius. To the north of the Chagos Archipelago are <a href="/wiki/Peros_Banhos" title="Peros Banhos">Peros Banhos</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Salomon_Islands" title="Salomon Islands">Salomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nelsons_Island" title="Nelsons Island">Nelsons Island</a>; to the south-west are <a href="/wiki/Three_Brothers,_Chagos" title="Three Brothers, Chagos">The Three Brothers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eagle_Islands" title="Eagle Islands">Eagle Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egmont_Islands" title="Egmont Islands">Egmont Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danger_Island,_Great_Chagos_Bank" title="Danger Island, Great Chagos Bank">Danger Island</a>. <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a> is in the south-east of the Archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-PCA_Memorial_Vol_1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCA_Memorial_Vol_1-14">[12]</a></sup> In 2016, the Chagossian population was estimated at 8,700 in Mauritius, including 483 natives; 350 Chagossians live in the Seychelles, including 75 natives, while 3,000, including 127 natives, live in the UK (the population having grown from the 1200 Chagossians who moved there).<sup id="cite_ref-chif_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chif-100">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Brandon">St. Brandon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: St. Brandon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/St._Brandon" title="St. Brandon">St. Brandon</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/St._Brandon" title="St. Brandon">St. Brandon</a>, also known as Cargados Carajos Shoals, is located 402 kilometres (250&nbsp;mi) northeast of Mauritius Island. The archipelago consists of 16 Islands and Islets. Saint Brandon consists of five island groups, with about 28–40 islands and islets in total, depending on seasonal storms and related sand movements. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Agal.C3.A9ga_Islands"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Agaléga_Islands">Agaléga Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Agaléga Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agal%C3%A9ga" title="Agaléga">Agaléga</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The twin islands of <a href="/wiki/Agal%C3%A9ga" title="Agaléga">Agaléga</a> are located some 1,000 kilometres (600 miles) to the north of Mauritius.<sup id="cite_ref-territory_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-territory-98">[96]</a></sup> Its North Island is 12.5&nbsp;km (<span class="frac nowrap">7<span class="visualhide">&nbsp;</span><sup>3</sup>⁄<sub>4</sub></span>&nbsp;mi) long and 1.5&nbsp;km (<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>7</sup>⁄<sub>8</sub></span>&nbsp;mi) wide, while its South Island is 7 by 4.5&nbsp;km (<span class="frac nowrap">4<span class="visualhide">&nbsp;</span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>4</sub></span> by <span class="frac nowrap">2<span class="visualhide">&nbsp;</span><sup>3</sup>⁄<sub>4</sub></span>&nbsp;mi). The total area of both islands is 26&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (10&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). According to Statistics Mauritius, at 1 July 2019, the population of Agaléga and St. Brandon was estimated at 274.<sup id="cite_ref-1_July_2019_Statistics_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1_July_2019_Statistics-99">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tromelin">Tromelin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tromelin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tromelin_Island" title="Tromelin Island">Tromelin Island</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tromelin_aerial_photograph.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Tromelin_aerial_photograph.JPG/220px-Tromelin_aerial_photograph.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Tromelin_aerial_photograph.JPG/330px-Tromelin_aerial_photograph.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Tromelin_aerial_photograph.JPG/440px-Tromelin_aerial_photograph.JPG 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tromelin_aerial_photograph.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Aerial view of Tromelin Island
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tromelin island lies 430&nbsp;km north-west of Mauritius. Mauritius claims sovereignty over <a href="/wiki/Tromelin_Island" title="Tromelin Island">Tromelin island</a>, as does France. </p>
      <p>The French took control of Mauritius in 1715, renaming it <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a>. France officially ceded Mauritius including all its dependencies to Britain through the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1814)" title="Treaty of Paris (1814)">Treaty of Paris</a>, signed on 30 May 1814 and in which <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> was returned to France. The <a href="/wiki/British_Mauritius" title="British Mauritius">British Colony of Mauritius</a> consisted of the main island of Mauritius along with its dependencies <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agalega" class="mw-redirect" title="Agalega">Agalega</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Brandon" class="mw-redirect" title="St Brandon">St Brandon</a>, Tromelin (disputed) and the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> became a separate colony in 1906. It is disputed whether the transfer of Isle de France (As Mauritius was previously known under French rule) and its dependencies to Britain in 1814 included Tromelin island. Article 8 of the Treaty of Paris stipulate the cession by France to Britain of Isle de France "and its dependencies, namely Rodrigues and the Seychelles". France considers that the sovereignty of Tromelin island was never transferred to Britain. Mauritius claims is based on the fact that the transfer of Isle de France and its dependencies to Britain in 1814 was general, it was beyond those called “namely” in the Treaty of Paris, all the dependencies of Isle de France were not specifically mentioned in the Treaty. Mauritius claim that since Tromelin was a dependency of Isle de France, it was 'de facto' transferred to Britain in 1814. In addition, the islands of Rodrigues, Agalega, St Brandon and the Chagos Archipelago were also not specifically mentioned in the Treaty of Paris but became part of the British Colony of Mauritius as they were dependencies of Isle de France at that time. In addition, the British authorities in Mauritius have been taking administrative measures with respect to Tromelin over the years, for instance, British officials granted four guano operating concessions on Tromelin island between 1901 and 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-tromelin_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tromelin-15">[13]</a></sup> In 1959, British officials in Mauritius informed the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> that it considered Tromelin to be part of its territory.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> A co-management treaty was reached by France and Mauritius in 2010 but has not been ratified.<sup id="cite_ref-diploma_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diploma-102">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts_of_Mauritius_Island">Districts of Mauritius Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Districts of Mauritius Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Mauritius" title="Districts of Mauritius">Districts of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Mauritius is subdivided into nine Districts, they consist of different <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities,_towns_and_villages_in_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities, towns and villages in Mauritius">cities, towns and villages</a>. </p> 
      <div role="img" class="noresize" style="width: 450px; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative;">

       </div>

        <b><a href="/wiki/Flacq_District" title="Flacq District">Flacq</a></b>
       </div>

       </div> 
       <div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:162px; top:176px">
        <b><a href="/wiki/Port_Louis_District" title="Port Louis District">Port Louis</a></b>
       </div>

       </div>

        <b><a href="/wiki/Moka_District" title="Moka District">Moka</a></b>
       </div>

      <p><br> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_disputes">Territorial disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Territorial disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chagos_Archipelago_2">Chagos Archipelago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Chagos Archipelago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago_sovereignty_dispute" title="Chagos Archipelago sovereignty dispute">Chagos Archipelago sovereignty dispute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Chagossians" title="Expulsion of the Chagossians">Expulsion of the Chagossians</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chagos_map.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Chagos_map.PNG/220px-Chagos_map.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Chagos_map.PNG/330px-Chagos_map.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Chagos_map.PNG/440px-Chagos_map.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1581" data-file-height="1768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chagos_map.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mauritius has long sought sovereignty over the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a>, located 1,287&nbsp;km (800&nbsp;mi) to the north-east. Chagos was administratively part of Mauritius from the 18th century when the French first settled the islands. All of the islands forming part of the French colonial territory of <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a> (as Mauritius was then known) were ceded to the British in 1810 under the Act of Capitulation signed between the two powers.<sup id="cite_ref-real_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-real-103">[101]</a></sup> In 1965, three years before the independence of Mauritius, the United Kingdom split the Chagos Archipelago from Mauritius and the islands of <a href="/wiki/Aldabra" title="Aldabra">Aldabra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farquhar_Group" title="Farquhar Group">Farquhar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desroches" class="mw-redirect" title="Desroches">Desroches</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> (BIOT). The islands were formally established as an overseas territory of the United Kingdom on 8 November 1965. On 23 June 1976, Aldabra, Farquhar and Desroches were returned to <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> as a result of its attaining independence. The BIOT now comprises the Chagos Archipelago only. The UK leased the main island of the archipelago, <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a>, to the United States under a 50-year lease to establish a military base.<sup id="cite_ref-real_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-real-103">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> In 2016, Britain unilaterally extended the lease to the US till 2036.<sup id="cite_ref-THE_HINDU_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_HINDU-105">[103]</a></sup> Mauritius has repeatedly asserted that the separation of its territories is a violation of United Nations resolutions banning the dismemberment of colonial territories before independence and claims that the Chagos Archipelago, including Diego Garcia, forms an integral part of the territory of Mauritius under both Mauritian law and international law.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> After initially denying that the islands were inhabited, British officials forcibly expelled to the mainland approximately 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Chagossians" title="Chagossians">Chagossians</a> who had lived on those islands for a century. To force the inhabitants to leave, first the British authorities cut off food supplies, and those who resisted were threatened with being shot or bombed if they did not leave the island. To frighten them, their dogs and pets were cruelly gassed to death.<sup id="cite_ref-dog_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dog-107">[105]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and in statements to its Parliament, the UK pretended that there was no "permanent population" in the Chagos Archipelago and described the population as mere "contract labourers" who were relocated.<sup id="cite_ref-ICJ_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICJ-11">[9]</a></sup> Since 1971, only the atoll of Diego Garcia is inhabited, home to some 3,000 UK and US military and civilian contracted personnel. Chagossians have since engaged in activism to return to the archipelago, claiming that their forced expulsion and dispossession were illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-108">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Section 111 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mauritius" title="Constitution of Mauritius">Constitution of Mauritius</a> states that “Mauritius” includes<sup id="cite_ref-con_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-con-110">[108]</a></sup> – </p>
      <p>(a) the Islands of Mauritius, Rodrigues, Agalega, Tromelin, Cargados Carajos and the Chagos Archipelago, including Diego Garcia and any other island comprised in the State of Mauritius; </p>
      <p>(b) the territorial sea and the air space above the territorial sea and the islands specified in paragraph (a); </p>
      <p>(c) the continental shelf; and </p>
      <p>(d) such places or areas as may be designated by regulations made by the Prime Minister, rights over which are or may become exercisable by Mauritius. </p>
      <p>Mauritius considers the territorial sea of the Chagos Archipelago and Tromelin island as part of its <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Maps_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maps-111">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Permanent Court of Arbitration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg/220px-Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="257" data-file-height="360"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The military base of <a href="/wiki/Camp_Justice_(Diego_Garcia)" title="Camp Justice (Diego Garcia)">Camp Justice</a> on <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 20 December 2010, Mauritius initiated proceedings against the United Kingdom under the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_on_the_Law_of_the_Sea" title="United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea">United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea</a> (UNCLOS) to challenge the legality of the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Marine_Protected_Area" title="Chagos Marine Protected Area">Chagos Marine Protected Area</a> (MPA), which the UK purported to declare around the Chagos Archipelago in April 2010. The dispute was arbitrated by the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration" title="Permanent Court of Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</a>. </p>
      <p>The sovereignty of Mauritius was explicitly recognized by two of the arbitrators and denied by none of the other three. Three members of the Tribunal found that they did not have jurisdiction to rule on that question; they expressed no view as to which of the two States has sovereignty over the Chagos Archipelago. Tribunal Judges <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCdiger_Wolfrum" title="Rüdiger Wolfrum">Rüdiger Wolfrum</a> and James Kateka held that the Tribunal did have jurisdiction to decide this question, and concluded that UK does not have sovereignty over the Chagos Archipelago. They found that:<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>internal United Kingdom documents suggested an ulterior motive behind the MPA, noting disturbing similarities and a common pattern between the establishment of the so-called "BIOT" in 1965 and the proclamation of the MPA in 2010;</li> 
       <li>the excision of the Chagos Archipelago from Mauritius in 1965 shows a complete disregard for the territorial integrity of Mauritius by the UK;</li> 
       <li>UK Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>'s threat to Premier <a href="/wiki/Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam">Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam</a> in 1965 that he could return home without independence if he did not consent to the excision of the Chagos Archipelago amounted to duress; Mauritian Ministers were coerced into agreeing to the detachment of the Chagos Archipelago, which violated the international law of self-determination;</li> 
       <li>the MPA is legally invalid.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The Tribunal's decision determined that the UK's undertaking to return the Chagos Archipelago to Mauritius gives Mauritius an interest in significant decisions that bear upon possible future uses of the Archipelago. The result of the Tribunal's decision is that it is now open to the Parties to enter into the negotiations that the Tribunal would have expected prior to the proclamation of the MPA, with a view to achieving a mutually satisfactory arrangement for protecting the marine environment, to the extent necessary under a "sovereignty umbrella".<sup id="cite_ref-cha_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cha-113">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Court_of_Justice">International Court of Justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: International Court of Justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Amendment_of_exclusion_clause_by_UK">Amendment of exclusion clause by UK</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Amendment of exclusion clause by UK">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <p>In 2004, following the decision of the British government to promulgate the British Indian Ocean Territory Order, which prohibited the <a href="/wiki/Chagossians" title="Chagossians">Chagossians</a> from remaining on the islands without express authorisation, Mauritius contemplated recourse to the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> to finally and conclusively settle the dispute. However, article 36 of the International Court of Justice Statute provides that it is the option of the state whether it wishes to subject itself to the court's jurisdiction. Where the state chooses to be so bound, it may also restrict or limit the jurisdiction of the court in a number of ways. The UK's clause deposited at the court excluded, amongst other things, the jurisdiction of the court with regard "to any disputes with the government of any country which is a member of the Commonwealth with regard to situations or facts existing before 1 January 1969". The temporal limitation of 1 January 1969 was inserted to exclude all disputes arising during decolonisation. The effect of the British exclusionary clause would thus have prevented Mauritius from resorting to the court on the Chagos dispute because it is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>. When Mauritius threatened to leave the Commonwealth, the United Kingdom quickly amended its exclusion clause to exclude any disputes between itself, Commonwealth States and <i>former Commonwealth States</i>, thereby quashing any Mauritian hopes to ever have recourse to the contentious jurisdiction of the court, even if it left.<sup id="cite_ref-commonwealth_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commonwealth-114">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Advisory_opinion">Advisory opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Advisory opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <p>On 22 June 2017, by a margin of 94 to 15 countries, the <a href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="UN General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> asked the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> to give an advisory opinion on the separation of the Chagos Archipelago from Mauritius before the country's independence in the 1960s. In September 2018, the International Court of Justice began hearings on the case. 17 countries have argued in favour of Mauritius.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The UK apologised for the "shameful" way islanders were evicted from the Chagos Archipelago but were insistent that Mauritius was wrong to bring the dispute over sovereignty of the strategic atoll group to the United Nations’ highest court.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> The UK and its allies argued that this matter should not be decided by the court but should be resolved through bilateral negotiations, while bilateral discussions with Mauritius have been unfruitful over the past 50 years. </p>
      <p>On 25 February 2019, the judges of the International Court of Justice by thirteen votes to one stated that the United Kingdom is under an obligation to bring to an end its administration of the Chagos Archipelago as rapidly as possible. Only the American judge, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Donoghue" title="Joan Donoghue">Joan Donoghue</a>, voted in favor of the UK. The president of the court, <a href="/wiki/Abdulqawi_Ahmed_Yusuf" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdulqawi Ahmed Yusuf">Abdulqawi Ahmed Yusuf</a>, said the detachment of the Chagos Archipelago in 1965 from Mauritius had not been based on a "free and genuine expression of the people concerned." "This continued administration constitutes a wrongful act," he said, adding "The UK has an obligation to bring to an end its administration of the Chagos Archipelago as rapidly as possible and that all member states must co-operate with the United Nations to complete the decolonization of Mauritius."<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 May 2019, the UK Foreign Office minister <a href="/wiki/Alan_Duncan" title="Alan Duncan">Alan Duncan</a> stated that Mauritius has never held sovereignty over the archipelago and the UK does not recognise its claim. He stated that the ruling was merely an advisory opinion and not a legally binding judgment. <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>, leader of the UK's main opposition party, wrote to the UK PM condemning her decision to defy a ruling of the UN's principal court that concluded that Britain should hand back the Chagos Islands to Mauritius. He expressed his concern that the UK government appears ready to disregard <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> and ignore a ruling of the international court and the right of the Chagossians to return to their homes.<sup id="cite_ref-Alan_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alan-119">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 22 May 2019, the United Nations General Assembly debated and adopted a resolution that affirmed that the Chagos Archipelago, which has been occupied by the UK for more than 50 years, "forms an integral part of the territory of Mauritius". The resolution gives effect to an advisory opinion of the International Court of Justice (ICJ), demanded that the UK "withdraw its colonial administration ... unconditionally within a period of no more than six months". 116 states voted in favour of the resolution, 55 abstained and only Australia, Hungary, Israel and Maldives supported the UK and US. During the debate, the Mauritian Prime Minister described the expulsion of Chagossians as "a <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crime against humanity</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Resolution_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resolution-120">[118]</a></sup> While the resolution is not legally binding, it carries significant political weight since the ruling came from the UN's highest court and the assembly vote reflects world opinion.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> The resolution also has immediate practical consequences: the UN, its specialised agencies, and all other international organisations are now bound, as a matter of UN law, to support the decolonisation of Mauritius even if the UK claim that it has no doubt about its sovereignty.<sup id="cite_ref-Resolution_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resolution-120">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Mauritius" title="Wildlife of Mauritius">Wildlife of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png/220px-Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png/330px-Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png/440px-Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png 2x" data-file-width="1298" data-file-height="974"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mauritius_ornate_day_gecko" title="Mauritius ornate day gecko">Mauritius ornate day gecko</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country is home to some of the world's rarest plants and animals, but human habitation and the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Non-native_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-native species">non-native species</a> have threatened its indigenous flora and fauna.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-108">[106]</a></sup> Due to its volcanic origin, age, isolation, and unique terrain, Mauritius is home to a diversity of flora and fauna not usually found in such a small area. Before the Portuguese arrival in 1507, there were no terrestrial mammals on the island. This allowed the evolution of a number of flightless birds and large reptile species. The arrival of humans saw the introduction of invasive alien species, the rapid destruction of habitat and the loss of much of the endemic flora and fauna. Less than 2% of the <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">native forest</a> now remains, concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park" title="Black River Gorges National Park">Black River Gorges National Park</a> in the south-west, the Bambous Mountain Range in the south-east, and the Moka-Port Louis Ranges in the north-west. There are some isolated mountains, <a href="/wiki/Corps_de_Garde" title="Corps de Garde">Corps de Garde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le_Morne_Brabant" title="Le Morne Brabant">Le Morne Brabant</a>, and several <a href="/wiki/Islets_of_Mauritius" title="Islets of Mauritius">offshore islands</a>, with remnants of coastal and mainland diversity. Over 100 species of plants and animals have become extinct and many more are threatened. Conservation activities began in the 1980s with the implementation of programmes for the reproduction of threatened bird and plant species as well as habitat restoration in the national parks and nature reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, the Ministry of Environment &amp; Sustainable Development issued the "Mauritius Environment Outlook Report," which recommended that St Brandon be declared a Marine Protected Area. </p>
      <p>In the President's Report of the <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Wildlife_Foundation" title="Mauritian Wildlife Foundation">Mauritian Wildlife Foundation</a> dated March 2016, St Brandon is declared an official MWF project in order to promote the conservation of the atoll.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_flying_fox" title="Mauritian flying fox">Mauritian Flying Fox</a> is the only remaining mammal endemic to the island, and has been severely threatened in recent years due to the government sanctioned culling introduced in November 2015 due to the belief that they were a threat to fruit plantations. Prior to 2015 the lack of severe cyclone had seen the fruit bat population increase and the status of the species was then changed by the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">IUCN</a> from Endangered to Vulnerable in 2014. October 2018, saw the authorisation of the cull of 20% of the fruit bat population, amounting to 13,000 of the estimated 65,000 fruit bats remaining, although their status had already reverted to Endangered due to the previous years' culls.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Dodo">The Dodo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: The Dodo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">Dodo</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/220px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/330px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/440px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2096" data-file-height="2240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mauritius was the only known habitat of the extinct <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a>, a flightless bird.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>When it was discovered, Mauritius was the home of a previously unknown species of bird, the <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a>, descendants of a type of <a href="/wiki/Pigeon" class="mw-redirect" title="Pigeon">pigeon</a> which settled in Mauritius over four million years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> With no predators to attack them, they had lost their ability to fly. The Portuguese discovered the island around 1505 and the island quickly became a stopover for ships engaged in the spice trade. Weighing up to 23&nbsp;kg (50&nbsp;lb), the dodo was a welcome source of fresh meat for the sailors. Large numbers of dodos were killed for food. Later, when the Dutch used the island as a penal colony, new species were introduced to the island. <a href="/wiki/Rat" title="Rat">Rats</a>, pigs, and <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">monkeys</a> ate dodo eggs in the ground nests. The combination of human exploitation and introduced species significantly reduced the dodo population. Within 100 years of the arrival of humans on Mauritius, the once abundant dodo became a rare bird. The last one was killed in 1681.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> The dodo is prominently featured as a (heraldic) <a href="/wiki/Supporter" title="Supporter">supporter</a> of the national <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Mauritius" title="Coat of arms of Mauritius">coat of arms of Mauritius</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_and_climate">Environment and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Environment and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Black_River_Gorges_National_Park,_Mauritius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg/220px-Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg/330px-Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg/440px-Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Black_River_Gorges_National_Park,_Mauritius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Black River Gorges National Park
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The environment in Mauritius is typically tropical in the coastal regions with forests in the mountainous areas. Seasonal cyclones are destructive to its flora and fauna, although they recover quickly. Mauritius ranked second in an <a href="/wiki/Air_quality_index" title="Air quality index">air quality index</a> released by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 5.46/10, ranking it 100<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-129">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Situated near the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">Tropic of Capricorn</a>, Mauritius has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a>. There are 2 seasons: a warm humid summer from November to April, with a mean temperature of 24.7&nbsp;°C (76.5&nbsp;°F) and a relatively cool dry winter from June to September with a mean temperature of 20.4&nbsp;°C (68.7&nbsp;°F). The temperature difference between the seasons is only 4.3<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>°C (7.7<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>°F). The warmest months are January and February with average day maximum temperature reaching 29.2&nbsp;°C (84.6&nbsp;°F) and the coolest months are July and August with average overnight minimum temperatures of 16.4&nbsp;°C (61.5&nbsp;°F). Annual rainfall ranges from 900&nbsp;mm (35&nbsp;in) on the coast to 1,500&nbsp;mm (59&nbsp;in) on the central plateau. Although there is no marked rainy season, most of the rainfall occurs in summer months. Sea temperature in the lagoon varies from 22–27&nbsp;°C (72–81&nbsp;°F). The central plateau is much cooler than the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Coastal" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastal">coastal</a> areas and can experience as much as double the rainfall. The prevailing trade winds keep the east side of the island cooler and bring more rain. Occasional <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclones" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical cyclones">tropical cyclones</a> generally occur between January and March and tend to disrupt the weather for about three days, bringing heavy rain.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pravind_Jugnauth" title="Pravind Jugnauth">Pravind Jugnauth</a> declared an environmental state of emergency after the July 25, <a href="/wiki/2020_in_East_Africa" title="2020 in East Africa">2020</a> <a href="/wiki/MV_Wakashio_oil_spill" title="MV Wakashio oil spill"><i>MV Wakashio</i> oil spill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> France sent aircraft and specialists from <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> said that the leak threatened the survival of thousands of species, who are at "risk of drowning in a sea of pollution".<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Mauritius" title="Politics of Mauritius">Politics of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG/220px-Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG/330px-Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG/440px-Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2567" data-file-height="1615"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Government House, Port Louis
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The politics of Mauritius take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic, in which the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mauritius" title="President of Mauritius">President</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius" title="Prime Minister of Mauritius">Prime Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, assisted by a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Ministers_of_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet of Ministers of Mauritius">Council of Ministers</a>. Mauritius has a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the Government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the Government and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Mauritius">National Assembly</a>. </p>
      <p>The National Assembly is Mauritius's <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> legislature, which was called the Legislative Assembly until 1992, when the country became a republic. It consists of 70 members, 62 elected for four-year terms in multi-member <a href="/wiki/Constituency" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituency">constituencies</a> and eight additional members, known as "best losers", appointed by the Electoral Service Commission to ensure that ethnic and religious minorities are equitably represented. The UN Human Rights Committee (UNHRC), which monitors member states' compliance with the International Covenant on Political and Civil Rights (ICPCR), has criticised the country's Best Loser System following a complaint by a local youth and trade union movement.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> The president is elected for a five-year term by the Parliament. </p>
      <p>The island of Mauritius is divided into <a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Mauritius" title="Constituencies of Mauritius">20 constituencies</a> that return three members each. The island of Rodrigues is a single district that returns two members. </p>
      <p>After a general election, the Electoral Supervisory Commission may nominate up to eight additional members with a view to correct any imbalance in the representation of ethnic minorities in Parliament. This system of nominating members is commonly called the best loser system. </p>
      <p>The political party or party alliance that wins the majority of seats in Parliament forms the government. Its leader becomes the Prime Minister, who selects the Cabinet from elected members of the Assembly, except for the Attorney General, who may not be an elected member of the Assembly. The political party or alliance which has the second largest group of representatives forms the Official Opposition and its leader is normally nominated by the President of the Republic as the Leader of the Opposition. The Assembly elects a Speaker, a Deputy Speaker and a Deputy Chairman of Committees as some of its first tasks. </p>
      <p>Mauritius is a democracy with a government elected every five years. The most recent National Assembly Election was held on 10 December 2014 in all the 20 mainland constituencies, and in the constituency covering the island of Rodrigues. Elections have tended to be a contest between two major coalitions of parties. </p>
      <p>The 2018 <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a> ranked Mauritius first in good governance.<sup id="cite_ref-Ibrahim_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibrahim-134">[132]</a></sup> According to the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> compiled by the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a> that measures the state of democracy in 167 countries, Mauritius ranks 16th worldwide and is the only African-related country with "full democracy".<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Mauritius">Military of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <p>All military, police, and security functions in Mauritius are carried out by 10,000 active-duty personnel under the Commissioner of Police. The 8,000-member National Police Force is responsible for domestic law enforcement. The 1,400-member <a href="/wiki/Special_Mobile_Force" title="Special Mobile Force">Special Mobile Force</a> (SMF) and the 688-member National Coast Guard are the only two paramilitary units in Mauritius. Both units are composed of police officers on lengthy rotations to those services.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Mauritius" title="Foreign relations of Mauritius">Foreign relations of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Prime_Minister,_Shri_Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius,_Mr._Pravind_Jugnauth,_on_the_sidelines_of_CHOGM_2018,_in_London_on_April_19,_2018_(2).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius%2C_Mr._Pravind_Jugnauth%2C_on_the_sidelines_of_CHOGM_2018%2C_in_London_on_April_19%2C_2018_%282%29.JPG/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius%2C_Mr._Pravind_Jugnauth%2C_on_the_sidelines_of_CHOGM_2018%2C_in_London_on_April_19%2C_2018_%282%29.JPG/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius%2C_Mr._Pravind_Jugnauth%2C_on_the_sidelines_of_CHOGM_2018%2C_in_London_on_April_19%2C_2018_%282%29.JPG/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1418" data-file-height="776"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Prime_Minister,_Shri_Narendra_Modi_meeting_the_Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius,_Mr._Pravind_Jugnauth,_on_the_sidelines_of_CHOGM_2018,_in_London_on_April_19,_2018_(2).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pravind_Jugnauth" title="Pravind Jugnauth">Pravind Jugnauth</a> with Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a>, 19 April 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mauritius has strong and friendly relations with various African, American, Asian, European and Oceania countries. Considered part of Africa geographically, Mauritius has friendly relations with African states in the region, particularly South Africa, by far its largest continental trading partner. Mauritian investors are gradually entering African markets, notably Madagascar, Mozambique and Zimbabwe. The country's political heritage and dependence on Western markets have led to close ties with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and its member states, particularly France. Relations with India is very strong for both historical and commercial reasons. Mauritius established diplomatic relations with China in April 1972 and was forced to defend this decision, along with naval contracts with the USSR in the same year. It has also been extending its Middle East outreach with the setting up of an embassy in Saudi Arabia<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> whose Ambassador also doubles as the country's ambassador to Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mauritius is a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa_Development_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Africa Development Community">Southern Africa Development Community</a> (SADC), the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Commission" title="Indian Ocean Commission">Indian Ocean Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/COMESA" class="mw-redirect" title="COMESA">COMESA</a>, and formed the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Rim_Association" title="Indian Ocean Rim Association">Indian Ocean Rim Association</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Legal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Mauritius has a hybrid legal system derived from <a href="/wiki/British_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="British common law">British common law</a> and the <a href="/wiki/French_civil_law" class="mw-redirect" title="French civil law">French civil law</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mauritius" title="Constitution of Mauritius">Constitution of Mauritius</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> and guaranteed the protection of the fundamental rights and freedoms of the individual. Mauritius has a single-structured judicial system consisting of two tiers, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Mauritius" title="Supreme Court of Mauritius">Supreme Court</a> and subordinate courts. The Supreme Court is composed of various divisions exercising jurisdiction such as the Master's Court, the Family Division, the Commercial Division (Bankruptcy), the Criminal Division, the Mediation Division, the Court of First Instance in civil and criminal proceedings, the Appellate jurisdiction: the Court of Civil Appeal and the Court of Criminal Appeal. Subordinate courts consist of the Intermediate Court, the Industrial Court, the District Courts, the Bail and Remand Court and the Court of Rodrigues. The <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> is the final court of appeal of Mauritius. After the independence of Mauritius in 1968, Mauritius maintained the Privy Council as its highest court of appeal. Appeals to the Judicial Committee from decisions of the Court of Appeal or the Supreme Court may be as of right or with the leave of the Court, as set out in section 81 of the Constitution and section 70A of the Courts Act. The Judicial Committee may also grant special leave to appeal from the decision of any court in any civil or criminal matter as per section 81(5) of the Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-141">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Mauritius" title="Demographics of Mauritius">Demographics of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg/220px-Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg/330px-Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg/440px-Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="425" data-file-height="389"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">Population pyramid</a> of Mauritius according to 2011 census
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The estimated population of the Republic of Mauritius was at 1,265,985, of whom 626,341 were males and 639,644 females as at 1 July 2019. The population on the island of Mauritius was 1,222,340, and that of Rodrigues island was 43,371; Agalega and Saint Brandon had an estimated total population of 274.<sup id="cite_ref-1_July_2019_Statistics_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1_July_2019_Statistics-99">[97]</a></sup> Mauritius has the second highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_population_density" title="List of African countries by population density">population density</a> in Africa. Subsequent to a Constitutional amendment in 1982, there is no need for Mauritians to reveal their ethnic identities for the purpose of population census. Official statistics on ethnicity are not available. The 1972 census was the last one to measure ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> Mauritius is a <a href="/wiki/Multiracial" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiracial">multiethnic</a> society, drawn from <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_of_Indian_origin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauritian of Indian origin">Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creoles" title="Mauritian Creoles">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_of_Chinese_origin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauritian of Chinese origin">Chinese</a> and European (mostly <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_of_French_origin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauritian of French origin">French</a>) origin. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Mauritius" title="Religion in Mauritius">Religion in Mauritius</a>

         </div>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2011 census conducted by <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Mauritius" title="Statistics Mauritius">Statistics Mauritius</a>, 48.5% of the Mauritian population follows <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (32.7%), <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (17.2%) and other religions (0.7%). 0.7% reported themselves as <a href="/wiki/Irreligiosity" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligiosity">non-religious</a> and 0.1% did not answer.<sup id="cite_ref-2011_Census_Religion_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Census_Religion-144">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Mauritius" title="Languages of Mauritius">Languages of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>

           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole" title="Mauritian Creole">Creole</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:Aquamarine; width:84%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">84%</td>
