          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:Aquamarine; width:7.1%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">7.1%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_language" title="Bhojpuri language">Bhojpuri</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:Aquamarine; width:5.3%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">5.3%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:Aquamarine; width:3.6%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3.6%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mauritius" title="Constitution of Mauritius">Mauritian constitution</a> makes no mention of an <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>. The Constitution only mentions that the official language of the National Assembly is <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>; however, any member can also address the chair in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-language_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-language-3">[2]</a></sup> English and French are generally considered to be de facto national and common languages of Mauritius, as they are the languages of government administration, courts, and business.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> The constitution of Mauritius is written in English, while some laws, such as the <a href="/wiki/Civil_code" title="Civil code">Civil code</a> and <a href="/wiki/Criminal_code" title="Criminal code">Criminal code</a>, are in French. The Mauritian currency features the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_script" title="Tamil script">Tamil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Devanagari_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Devanagari script">Devanagari scripts</a>. </p>
      <p>The Mauritian population is <a href="/wiki/Multilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Multilingual">multilingual</a>; while <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole" title="Mauritian Creole">Mauritian Creole</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother tongue">mother tongue</a> of most Mauritians, most people are also fluent in English and French; they tend to switch languages according to the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> French and English are favoured in educational and professional settings, while <a href="/wiki/Asian_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian languages">Asian languages</a> are used mainly in music, religious and cultural activities. The media and literature are primarily in French. </p>
      <p>The Creole language, which is <a href="/wiki/French-based_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="French-based Creole">French-based</a> with some additional influences, is spoken by the majority of the population as a native language.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> The Creole languages which are spoken in different islands of the country are more or less similar: <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole" title="Mauritian Creole">Mauritian Creole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rodriguan_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodriguan Creole">Rodriguan Creole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agalega_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Agalega Creole">Agalega Creole</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chagossian_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Chagossian Creole">Chagossian Creole</a> are spoken by people from the islands of Mauritius, <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agalega" class="mw-redirect" title="Agalega">Agalega</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chagos" class="mw-redirect" title="Chagos">Chagos</a>. Some ancestral languages that are also spoken in Mauritius include <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-chinese_act_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinese_act-149">[147]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hindi_act_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hindi_act-150">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-marathi_act_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marathi_act-151">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-tamil_act_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tamil_act-152">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a><sup id="cite_ref-telegu_act_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegu_act-153">[151]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-urdu_act_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urdu_act-154">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a>, once widely spoken as a mother tongue, has become less commonly spoken over the years. According to the 2011 census, Bhojpuri was spoken by 5% of the population compared to 12% in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-2011census_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011census-5">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>School students must learn English and French; they may also opt for an Asian language or Mauritian Creole. The medium of instruction varies from school to school but is usually Creole, French and English. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Mauritius" title="Education in Mauritius">Education in Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The education system in Mauritius consists of pre-primary, primary, secondary and tertiary sectors. The education structure consists of two to three years of pre-primary school, six years of primary schooling leading to the Primary School Achievement Certificate, five years of secondary education leading to the School Certificate, and two years of higher secondary ending with the Higher School Certificate. Secondary schools have "college" as part of their title. The government of Mauritius provides <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education</a> to its citizens from pre-primary to tertiary level. In 2013 government expenditure on education was estimated at about ₨&nbsp;13,584&nbsp;million, representing 13% of total expenditure.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> As of January 2017, the government has introduced changes to the education system with the Nine-Year Continuous Basic Education programme, which abolished the Certificate of Primary Education (CPE).<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/O-Level" class="mw-redirect" title="O-Level">O-Level</a> and <a href="/wiki/A-Level" class="mw-redirect" title="A-Level">A-Level</a> examinations are carried out by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> through <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge_International_Examinations" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Cambridge International Examinations">University of Cambridge International Examinations</a>. The tertiary education sector includes universities and other technical institutions in Mauritius. The two main public universities are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mauritius" title="University of Mauritius">University of Mauritius</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Technology,_Mauritius" title="University of Technology, Mauritius">University of Technology</a>, in addition to the Université des Mascareignes, founded in 2012, and the Open University Mauritius. These four public universities and several other technical institutes and higher education colleges are tuition-free for students as of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> was estimated at 92.7% in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mauritius" title="Economy of Mauritius">Economy of Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_Mauritius" title="International rankings of Mauritius">International rankings of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_(reduced_colour_saturation).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg/220px-Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg/330px-Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg/440px-Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_(reduced_colour_saturation).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">Sugar cane</a> plantation in Mauritius
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since independence from Britain in 1968, Mauritius has developed from a low-income, agriculture-based economy to a <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income</a> diversified economy, based on <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Mauritius" title="Tourism in Mauritius">tourism</a>, textiles, sugar, and financial services. The economic history of Mauritius since independence has been called "the Mauritian Miracle" and the "success of Africa" (Romer, 1992; Frankel, 2010; Stiglitz, 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years, information and communication technology, seafood, hospitality and property development, healthcare, renewable energy, and <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Mauritius" title="Education in Mauritius">education</a> and training have emerged as important sectors, attracting substantial investment from both local and foreign investors.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mauritius has no exploitable fossil fuel reserves and so relies on petroleum products to meet most of its energy requirements. Local and renewable energy sources are biomass, hydro, solar and wind energy.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> The country will be potentially among the main winners after the global transition to renewable energy is completed; it is ranked no. 8 out of 156 countries in the index of geopolitical gains and losses after energy transition (GeGaLo Index).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mauritius has one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zones</a> in the world, and in 2012 the government announced its intention to develop the marine economy.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mauritius is ranked high in terms of economic competitiveness, a friendly investment climate, good governance and a free economy.<sup id="cite_ref-heritage_foundation_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heritage_foundation-164">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-State.gov_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State.gov-165">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Doing_business_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doing_business-166">[164]</a></sup> The Gross Domestic Product (PPP) was estimated at US$29.187 billion in 2018, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP (PPP) per capita</a> was over US$22,909, the second highest in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-heritage_foundation_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heritage_foundation-164">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-State.gov_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State.gov-165">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Doing_business_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doing_business-166">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mauritius has a <i><a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income economy</a></i>, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-WB_GROUP_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB_GROUP-20">[18]</a></sup> The World Bank's 2019 <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_Doing_Business_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Ease of Doing Business Index">Ease of Doing Business Index</a> ranks Mauritius 13th worldwide out of 190 economies in terms of ease of doing business. According to the Mauritian Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the country's challenges are heavy reliance on a few industry sectors, high brain drain, scarcity of skilled labour, ageing population and inefficient public companies and para-statal bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mauritius has built its success on a free market economy. According to the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Economic_Freedom_of_the_World" title="Economic Freedom of the World">Economic Freedom of the World</a> report, Mauritius is ranked as having the 9th most free economy in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Evening_Port_Louis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Evening_Port_Louis.jpg/220px-Evening_Port_Louis.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Evening_Port_Louis.jpg/330px-Evening_Port_Louis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Evening_Port_Louis.jpg/440px-Evening_Port_Louis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Evening_Port_Louis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Port-Louis" class="mw-redirect" title="Port-Louis">Port-Louis</a>, the capital of Mauritius.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Services_Commission_(Mauritius)" title="Financial Services Commission (Mauritius)">Financial Services Commission</a>, financial and insurance activities contributed to 11.1% of the country's GDP in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> Over the years, Mauritius has been positioning itself as the preferred hub for investment into Africa due its strategic location between Asia and Africa, hybrid regulatory framework, ease of doing business, investment protection treaties, non-double taxation treaties, highly qualified and multilingual workforce, political stability, low crime rate coupled with modern infrastructure and connectivity. It is home to a number of international banks, legal firms, corporate services, investment funds and private equity funds. Financial products and services, includes private banking, global business, insurance and reinsurance, limited companies, protected cell companies, trust and foundation, investment banking, global headquarter administration.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite being tagged as a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> by the press due to its low tax regime,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> the country has built up a solid reputation by making use of best practices and adopting a strong legal and regulatory framework to demonstrate its compliance with international demands for greater transparency. In June 2015, Mauritius adhered to the multilateral <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Mutual_Administrative_Assistance_in_Tax_Matters" title="Convention on Mutual Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters">Convention on Mutual Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters</a>, and currently has an exchange information mechanism with 127 jurisdictions. Mauritius is a founding member of the Eastern and Southern Africa Anti Money Laundering Group and has been at the forefront in the fight against money laundering and other forms of financial crime. The country has adopted exchange of information on an automatic basis under the <a href="/wiki/Common_Reporting_Standard" title="Common Reporting Standard">Common Reporting Standard</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Accounts_Tax_Compliance_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Accounts Tax Compliance Act">Foreign Accounts Tax Compliance Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-govt5_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt5-174">[172]</a></sup> Mauritius is not on the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> blacklist.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> Furthermore, Mauritius appears on the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> white list of jurisdictions that have substantially implemented the internationally agreed tax standards. The OECD white list looks at jurisdictions from multiple angles; tax transparency, fair taxation, the implementation of OECD BEPS measures and substance requirements for zero-tax countries.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Mauritius" title="Tourism in Mauritius">Tourism in Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_beach.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/220px-Mauritius_beach.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/330px-Mauritius_beach.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/440px-Mauritius_beach.png 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_beach.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A tropical beach in <a href="/wiki/Trou-aux-Biches" title="Trou-aux-Biches">Trou-aux-Biches</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mauritius is a major tourist destination, the tourism sector is the fourth contributor to the Mauritian economy. The island nation enjoys a tropical climate with clear warm sea waters, beaches, tropical fauna and flora complemented by a multi-ethnic and cultural population.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> The forecast of tourist arrivals for the year 2019 is maintained at 1,450,000, representing an increase of 3.6% over the figure of 1,399,408 in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-Tou_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tou-178">[176]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mauritius currently has two <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a>, namely, <a href="/wiki/Aapravasi_Ghat" title="Aapravasi Ghat">Aapravasi Ghat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Le_Morne_Brabant" title="Le Morne Brabant">Le Morne Cultural Landscape</a>. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park" title="Black River Gorges National Park">Black River Gorges National Park</a> is currently in the UNESCO tentative list.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Mauritius" title="Transport in Mauritius">Transport in Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Metro_Express_Mauritius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Metro_Express_Mauritius.jpg/220px-Metro_Express_Mauritius.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Metro_Express_Mauritius.jpg/330px-Metro_Express_Mauritius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Metro_Express_Mauritius.jpg/440px-Metro_Express_Mauritius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="2268"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Metro_Express_Mauritius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/CAF_Urbos" title="CAF Urbos">Urbos 100–3</a> at Rose Hill Central Station
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 2005 public buses in Mauritius have been free of charge for students, people with disabilities and senior citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> There is currently a railway project under construction in Mauritius, former privately owned industrial railways having been abandoned. The harbour of <a href="/wiki/Port_Louis" title="Port Louis">Port Louis</a> handles international trade as well as a cruise terminal. The sole international airport for civil aviation is <a href="/wiki/Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_International_Airport" title="Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam International Airport">Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam International Airport</a>, which also serves as the home operating base for the national airline <a href="/wiki/Air_Mauritius" title="Air Mauritius">Air Mauritius</a>; the airport authority inaugurated a new passenger terminal in September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> Another airport is the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Ga%C3%ABtan_Duval_Airport" title="Sir Gaëtan Duval Airport">Sir Gaëtan Duval Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a>. Mauritius has a serious traffic problem due to the high number of road users, particularly car drivers. To solve the traffic congestion issue, the government has embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Metro_Express_(Mauritius)" title="Metro Express (Mauritius)">Metro Express</a> project. The line starts from Port Louis and will go to Curepipe when completed. The first phase of the project was completed in January 2020 while the second phase will be completed in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_and_communications_technology">Information and communications technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Information and communications technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The information and communications technology (ICT) sector has contributed to 5.7% of its GDP in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup> Since 2016, Mauritius has participated in International Competitions led by cyberstorm.mu. They organized the 2016 &amp; 2017 Google Code-in in Mauritius leading to 2 finalists and 1 Grand Prize Winner.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> Additionally, they have participated in the Internet Engineering Task Force (<a href="/wiki/Internet_Engineering_Task_Force" title="Internet Engineering Task Force">IETF</a>) <a href="/wiki/Hackathon" title="Hackathon">hackathon</a> where they worked on <a href="/wiki/TLS_1.3" class="mw-redirect" title="TLS 1.3">TLS 1.3</a>, <a href="/wiki/HTTP_451" title="HTTP 451">HTTP 451</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secure_Shell" class="mw-redirect" title="Secure Shell">SSH</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> The community has been going strong since sometimes with the organisation of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://conference.mscc.mu">DevCon</a>, a free tech-inclusive 3-day conference with sponsors such as <a href="/wiki/JetBrains" title="JetBrains">JetBrains</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Commercial_Bank" title="Mauritius Commercial Bank">Mauritius Commercial Bank</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astek" class="extiw" title="fr:Astek">Astek</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Supinfo" title="Supinfo">SUPINFO</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ceridian" title="Ceridian">Ceridian</a><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> and <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/SD_Worx" class="extiw" title="fr:SD Worx">SDWorkx</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> It is the largest event for developers in Mauritius organised in conjunction with local usergroups. Local usergroups include the Front-end coders, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://gophers.mu/#/">GophersMU</a>, the Mauritius Makers Community, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.pymug.com">Python Mauritius User Group(PyMUG)</a> and the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://lugm.org">Linux User Group of Mauritius (LUGM)</a>. </p>
      <p>Additionally, the African Network Information Centre (<a href="/wiki/AFRINIC" title="AFRINIC">AFRINIC</a>) – the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Internet_registry" title="Regional Internet registry">regional Internet registry</a> for Africa – is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Ebene,_Mauritius" title="Ebene, Mauritius">Ebene</a>, Mauritius. </p>
      <p>Mauritius is also connected to global Internet infrastructure via multiple optical fibre <a href="/wiki/Submarine_communications_cable" title="Submarine communications cable">submarine communications cables</a>, including the Lower Indian Ocean Network (<a href="/wiki/LION_(cable_system)" title="LION (cable system)">LION</a>) cable, the <a href="/wiki/Mauritius%E2%80%93Rodrigues_Submarine_Cable" title="Mauritius–Rodrigues Submarine Cable">Mauritius–Rodrigues Submarine Cable</a>, and the South Africa Far East (<a href="/wiki/SAFE_(cable_system)" title="SAFE (cable system)">SAFE</a>) cable. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Mauritius" title="Culture of Mauritius">Culture of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Prominent Mauritian painters include Vaco Baissac,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Henri_Le_Sidaner" title="Henri Le Sidaner">Henri Le Sidaner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_de_Chazal" title="Malcolm de Chazal">Malcolm de Chazal</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_Wiehe" title="Gabrielle Wiehe">Gabrielle Wiehe</a> is a prominent illustrator and graphic designer. Mauritius is also the source of the <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_%22Post_Office%22_stamps" title="Mauritius &quot;Post Office&quot; stamps">Mauritius "Post Office" stamps</a>, among the rarest postage stamps in the world, last sold for $4 million, and considered "the greatest item in all philately" by some.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The distinctive architecture of Mauritius reflects the island nation's history as a colonial trade base connecting Europe with the East. Styles and forms introduced by Dutch, French, and British settlers from the seventeenth century onward, mixed with influences from India and East Africa, resulted in a unique hybrid architecture of international historic, social, and artistic significance. Mauritian structures present a variety of designs, materials, and decorative elements that are unique to the country and inform the historical context of the Indian Ocean and European colonialism.<sup id="cite_ref-wmf.org_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wmf.org-196">[194]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Decades of political, social, and economic change have resulted in the routine destruction of Mauritian architectural heritage. Between 1960 and 1980, the historic homes of the island's high grounds, known locally as campagnes, disappeared at alarming rates. More recent years have witnessed the demolition of plantations, residences, and civic buildings as they have been cleared or drastically renovated for new developments to serve an expanding tourism industry. The capital city of Port Louis remained relatively unchanged until the mid-1990s, yet now reflects the irreversible damage that has been inflicted on its built heritage. Rising land values are pitted against the cultural value of historic structures in Mauritius, while the prohibitive costs of maintenance and the steady decline in traditional building skills make it harder to invest in preservation.<sup id="cite_ref-wmf.org_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wmf.org-196">[194]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The general populace historically lived in what are termed creole houses.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_literature" title="Mauritian literature">Mauritian literature</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Prominent Mauritian writers include <a href="/wiki/Marie-Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_Humbert" title="Marie-Thérèse Humbert">Marie-Thérèse Humbert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_de_Chazal" title="Malcolm de Chazal">Malcolm de Chazal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ananda_Devi" title="Ananda Devi">Ananda Devi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenaz_Patel" title="Shenaz Patel">Shenaz Patel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khal_Torabully" title="Khal Torabully">Khal Torabully</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._M._G._Le_Cl%C3%A9zio" title="J. M. G. Le Clézio">J. M. G. Le Clézio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aqiil_Gopee" title="Aqiil Gopee">Aqiil Gopee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dev_Virahsawmy" title="Dev Virahsawmy">Dev Virahsawmy</a>. J. M. G. Le Clézio, who won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize for Literature">Nobel Prize for Literature</a> in 2008, is of Mauritian heritage and holds dual French-Mauritian citizenship. The island plays host to the Le Prince Maurice Prize. In keeping with the island's literary culture the prize alternates on a yearly basis between English-speaking and French-speaking writers. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mauritius" title="Music of Mauritius">Music of Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sega_(genre)" title="Sega (genre)">Sega (genre)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The major musical genres of Mauritius are <a href="/wiki/Sega_(genre)" title="Sega (genre)">Sega</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Fusion_genre" class="mw-redirect" title="Fusion genre">fusion genre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seggae" title="Seggae">Seggae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_language" title="Bhojpuri language">Bhojpuri</a> <a href="/wiki/Indian_folk_music" title="Indian folk music">folk songs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filmi" title="Filmi">Indian movie music</a> especially <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">Classical music</a> mainly <a href="/wiki/Western_classical_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Western classical music">Western classical music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Mauritius" title="Cuisine of Mauritius">Cuisine of Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Mauritius" title="Cuisine of Mauritius">cuisine of Mauritius</a> is a combination of Indian, Creole, French and Chinese, with many dishes unique to the island. Spices are also a major component of Mauritian cuisine. One famous drink originating from Mauritius is Alouda, a cold beverage made with milk, basil seeds, and agar-agar jelly. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays_and_festivals">Holidays and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Holidays and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The public holidays of Mauritius involve the blending of several cultures from Mauritius's history. There are <a href="/wiki/Hindu_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu festivals">Hindu festivals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese festivals">Chinese festivals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslim_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim festivals">Muslim festivals</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Christian_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian festivals">Christian festivals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup> There are 15 annual public holidays in Mauritius. All the public holidays related to religious festivals have dates that vary from year to year except for Christmas. Other festivals such as <a href="/wiki/Holi" title="Holi">Holi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raksha_Bandhan" title="Raksha Bandhan">Raksha Bandhan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durga_Puja" title="Durga Puja">Durga Puja</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jacques-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Laval" title="Jacques-Désiré Laval">Père Laval Pilgrimage</a> also enrich the cultural landscape of Mauritius. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maiden_Cup_2006,_Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse,_Port_Louis,_Mauritius_-_20060910.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Maiden_Cup_2006%2C_Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse%2C_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_-_20060910.jpg/220px-Maiden_Cup_2006%2C_Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse%2C_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_-_20060910.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Maiden_Cup_2006%2C_Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse%2C_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_-_20060910.jpg/330px-Maiden_Cup_2006%2C_Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse%2C_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_-_20060910.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Maiden_Cup_2006%2C_Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse%2C_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_-_20060910.jpg/440px-Maiden_Cup_2006%2C_Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse%2C_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_-_20060910.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a>

        </div>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Mauritius" title="Football in Mauritius">Football in Mauritius</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most popular sport in Mauritius is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup> and the national team is known as The <a href="/wiki/Dodos" class="mw-redirect" title="Dodos">Dodos</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_national_football_team" title="Mauritius national football team">Club M</a>. Other popular sports in Mauritius include cycling, table tennis, horse racing, badminton, volleyball, basketball, handball, boxing, judo, karate, taekwondo, weightlifting, bodybuilding and athletics. Water sports include swimming, sailing, scuba diving, windsurfing and <a href="/wiki/Kitesurfing" class="mw-redirect" title="Kitesurfing">kitesurfing</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred_horse_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Thoroughbred horse racing">Horseracing</a>, which dates from 1812 when the <a href="/wiki/Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse" title="Champ de Mars Racecourse">Champ de Mars Racecourse</a> was inaugurated, remains popular. The country hosted the second (1985), fifth (2003) and tenth editions (2019) of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Island_Games" title="Indian Ocean Island Games">Indian Ocean Island Games</a>. Mauritius won its first Olympic medal at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> in Beijing when boxer <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Julie" title="Bruno Julie">Bruno Julie</a> won the bronze medal. </p>
      <p>In golf, the former <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Open" title="Mauritius Open">Mauritius Open</a> and the current <a href="/wiki/AfrAsia_Bank_Mauritius_Open" title="AfrAsia Bank Mauritius Open">AfrAsia Bank Mauritius Open</a> have been part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="European Tour">European Tour</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mauritius" title="Constitution of Mauritius">Mauritian constitution</a> makes no mention of an <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>. The Constitution only mentions that the official language of the National Assembly is English; however, any member can also address the chair in French.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Language most often spoken at home, as per 2011 Census.</span> </li> 
        </ol>

                <th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%">Regions</th>
